  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_4d2d7726-3e7b-40ac-aea5-359cffe61689'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);
    };

<div class='communityAnswer'>
<div class='communityAnswerBody'>
<div class='answererUserIcon'>
<a class="leftAlignedImage userPhoto" href="/user/show/4060569-jill"><img alt="" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/f_100x100-6433b08cbe793211f55e184d39e84c4d.png" /></a>
</div>
<div class='communityAnswerTextContainer'>
<span class='communityAnswererName'>
<a rel="nofollow" href="/user/show/4060569-jill">Jill</a>
</span>
<span class='communityAnswerText'>
<div class='spoiler'>
This answer contains spoilers…
<span class='spoilerAnswerText'>
<a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[
  
    Some. Some. Maybe.<br /><br />A girl of the 3,000 years ago gets viciously but not graphically raped and they have to deal with the aftermath. A guy named Walker <a href="#" rel="nofollow noopener">…more</a>
    Some. Some. Maybe.<br /><br />A girl of the 3,000 years ago gets viciously but not graphically raped and they have to deal with the aftermath. A guy named Walker is identified with profanity. Some people fall in love. I'm not through reading it yet. Some of it's really good. What was hard for me is when a complication is waved in the air. So she sneezed. And she had a cold. And she sneezed again. And she sneezed on this guy. And thus was started a devastating plague that swept through all the locals. And that guy kind of makes our heroes uncomfortable, though he hasn't really done anything. Something about him makes them kind of uneasy. I'm up to the parts where he's starting to show his true colors, but not to them.<a href="#" rel="nofollow noopener">(less)</a>
  
 <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>
</span>
</div>
</span>

  <div class="friendReviews elementListBrown" >
    <div class="section firstReview">
      

<div id="review_61296221" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/61296221" />
    <a title="Brownbetty" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/274033-brownbetty"><img alt="Brownbetty" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1188228975p2/274033.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/61296221?book_show_action=true">Jun 27, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Brownbetty" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Brownbetty" href="/user/show/274033-brownbetty">Brownbetty</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer61296221" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7465369606860921771">This book is technically fairly well executed, but politically leaves me cross-eyed. Warning for sexual violence, weird race issues, and general ookiness. In order to discuss it, first, an overview of the plot:<br/><br/>One spring night, the island of Nantucket (with several miles of coastal waters) is inexplicably transported into the bronze age. Luckily for the islanders, the coastal waters include a Coast Guard ship, the <i>Eagle</i>, and her captain, Black lesbian Marian Alston, who is plenty competent to or</span>
  <span id="freeText7465369606860921771" style="display:none">This book is technically fairly well executed, but politically leaves me cross-eyed. Warning for sexual violence, weird race issues, and general ookiness. In order to discuss it, first, an overview of the plot:<br /><br />One spring night, the island of Nantucket (with several miles of coastal waters) is inexplicably transported into the bronze age. Luckily for the islanders, the coastal waters include a Coast Guard ship, the <i>Eagle</i>, and her captain, Black lesbian Marian Alston, who is plenty competent to organize the transportation needs of the island (which, given the island is not agriculturally self-sufficient, are legion.)<br /><br />The book covers Nantucket's efforts at self-preservation and adaptation to their new reality. This includes making contact and political agreements with the peoples around them, as well as their scramble to adapt their silicon-age technology to the bronze-age resources available to them.<br /><br />The book is both a gleeful [Book:Swiss Family Robinson] style pipe-dream of how one might adapt modern knowledge to stone-age resources, and an imperialist fantasy in a slightly self-consciously progressive language. It occasionally does very well at not being fucking offensive, only to make it extra obvious when it falls off the wagon.<br /><br />The one thing it does well at is not condescending to the Bronze Age inhabitants or their technology. Stirling acknowledges that their technology represents real and situation-appropriate innovation, and when they encounter the industrial technology of the islanders, quickly grasp its use and usefulness. A good part of the Nantucket islanders' technological advantage comes not from their modern technology, but from their libraries which allow them access to all the societies of history, and to pick and choose from their solutions to common problems.<br /><br />On the other hand... Oh dear god, where to start. The islanders manifestly need a staple, and the island being too small for their agriculture to support their population, their only option is trade, and they decide to contact the tribal civilizations they expect to find in England, in order to do this. In the book, their reasoning is that an islander who speaks Lithuanian is expected to be able to quickly learn the language spoken there, but this surely is the author rather than probability; I would have rated odds of finding someone who spoke Classical Greek higher than someone who spoke Lithuanian, and both agriculture and trade ought to be more, rather than less advanced in the Mediterranean.<br /><br />What about the near-by inhabitants of what, in the history they left, would have come to be called 'the Americas'? Wikipedia tells me the Olmecs had maize and sweet potatoes. In Stirling's books, however, the first contact with the the peoples of the mainland leads to unleashing the common cold on them, and devastating a tribe. The second is when a delusional hippie, attempting to give the Olmec some protection against what she regards as the inevitable incursion of and devastation by arming them. She is captured, and ceremonially raped by a jaguar as a precursor to being used as a human sacrifice. Later, we learn that the Olmec have been infected with mumps and will likely be wiped out.<br /><br />On what-would-be British Isles, the islanders come upon a conflict between the earlier inhabitants and the recent invaders (I think from what-would-be France, based on their names end with -ix, and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/122410.Asterix_and_Cleopatra" title="Asterix and Cleopatra by René Goscinny" rel="nofollow noopener">Asterix</a>) and find themselves sympathizing with the embattled locals, but trading with the victorious invaders, believing themselves to have no choice in order to survive. The invading people give the Islanders various treaty-gifts, included a captured slave-girl.<br /><br />Which is where the lesbian pirate-queen romance takes off, awesome! (Not really pirates, but good enough!) Marion Alston is likeable, and her romance with young Swindapa, awkward, sweet, and the epitome of cross-cultural, is fun. But Alston as a character is occasionally jarring when she seems to be speaking for the author, as when she encourages another young Black cadet to stop thinking of themselves as Black, since in a few generations their skin differences will disappear into the island population like a drop of coffee in a glass of milk. She also tells him that their decision to trade in England rather than Africa is necessary, since in the Egyptian courts, she and he would be treated as just as sub-human as their ancestors had been Confederate America. What about West Africa, though? It's closer than Egypt, and agriculturally established. I would have bought someone speaking Swahili as easily as I bought someone speaking Lithuanian, and wikipedia confirms my memory of a western Bantu culture in the relevant time culture. I don't actually think contacting the people of the contingently-British-Isles is unlikely, but I don't think it's something that can be defended as a purely disinterested and logical choice.<br /><br />The villains of the piece are also kind of icky, beyond mere villainy; Walker, a sailor, decides to take his knowledge of technology and use it to set himself up as an emperor in the Mediterranean. He takes with him a small party of like-minded people, including Alice Hong, a nurse who has been "Black-listed from every kink club on the East Coast", a sado-masochist who Walker dominates and who enjoys dominating the prisoners (slaves) Walker uses to build his civilization. It seems utterly gratuitous, a sort of dog-kicking to demonstrate villainy, and it doesn't help at all that she's the second most visible non-white character.<br /><br />Actually, written like this, it seems far more clearly problematic than it did to me while reading. While reading, it was mostly a vague discomfort, which I attributed to raised mindfulness as a result of mammothfail.</span>
  <a data-text-id="7465369606860921771" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_191655405" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/191655405" />
    <a title="Kat  Hooper" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2177891-kat-hooper"><img alt="Kat  Hooper" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1533675060p2/2177891.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/191655405?book_show_action=true">Jul 29, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kat  Hooper" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kat  Hooper" href="/user/show/2177891-kat-hooper">Kat  Hooper</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Audio CD 9781400136797" href="/book/show/8777528-island-in-the-sea-of-time">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2177891-kat-hooper?shelf=audiobook">audiobook</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer191655405" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3468705126847615250">ORIGINALLY POSTED AT <a href='http://www.fantasyliterature.com' rel='nofollow noopener'>Fantasy Literature</a>.<br/><br/>After a strange electrical storm, the residents of Nantucket discover that their entire island and its surrounding waters have been sent back to 1300 B.C. Now this society, which is mostly based on a tourist economy, must figure out how to establish a new identity in prehistory. This includes clearing and farming land, building ships, finding new sources of fuel, salt, and other necessities, and most difficult of all, developing a constitution and befriend</span>
  <span id="freeText3468705126847615250" style="display:none">ORIGINALLY POSTED AT <a href="http://www.fantasyliterature.com" rel="nofollow noopener">Fantasy Literature</a>.<br /><br />After a strange electrical storm, the residents of Nantucket discover that their entire island and its surrounding waters have been sent back to 1300 B.C. Now this society, which is mostly based on a tourist economy, must figure out how to establish a new identity in prehistory. This includes clearing and farming land, building ships, finding new sources of fuel, salt, and other necessities, and most difficult of all, developing a constitution and befriending native trading partners.<br /><br />Fortunately, Nantucket has some citizens with valuable knowledge and skills who find themselves naturally rising to leadership positions: a brave and competent Baptist police chief, a widely-read and level-headed librarian, a black lesbian ship captain, a history professor, an astronomy student, the manager of the local grocery store, and a Catholic priest.<br /><br />But of course there are also some citizens who cause problems: the church whose pastor teaches that sending Nantucket back in time was Satan’s plan to prevent the birth of Christ, and the “flake-and-nut contingent” who want to arm the natives so they’ll never be oppressed by future Americans. Then there’s the biggest threat of all — the ambitious Coast Guard Lieutenant William Walker who sees all this confusion as an opportunity to set up his very own kingdom.<br /><br />I have a thing for time-travel novels — especially the Survivor-style stories in which modern people are forced to live in more uncivilized and unsophisticated times. Island in the Sea of Time has the added fun of actually having modern conveniences but not having the power or fuel to run them. Thus, the people of Nantucket must disassemble their cars for sheet metal while raiding their museums for whaling and milling antiques.<br /><br />There’s more to this story than survival and industrial revolution, though. Island in the Sea of Time is full of characters who feel like real people — people you might actually know. For the most part their relationships and romances are believable and understandable as former strangers work together to create a new society. The villains, however, are over-the-top. It’s hard to believe in the doctor’s sadism, William Walker’s vast knowledge and foresight, and the granola crowds’ naiveté (their leader is shocked that the natives are “sexist,” “patriarchal,” and “abusive of animals” and that they don’t immediately trust the Americans).<br /><br />At times, Island in the Sea of Time becomes a bit teachy as characters discuss token economies, division of labor, ship building, linguistics, farming techniques, iron casting, steam engines, canning, the production of gunpowder, the use and care of firearms, etc. And it gets a little preachy as they discuss the creation of a new constitution. But generally I thought S.M. Stirling did a good job with this aspect of the book.<br /><br />I read the audio version of Island in the Sea of Time, narrated by Todd McLaren and produced by Tantor Audio. The best thing I can say about it is that I mostly forgot I was listening to an audiobook — McLaren’s voices and cadences were so natural that they never called attention to themselves. The only time I was brought out of the story was when McLaren used his “Boston” voice for the U. Mass astronomy intern. But that’s not McLaren’s fault...<br /><br />Island in the Sea of Time comes to a satisfactory end, but most readers will be eager to continue the islanders’ advances and adventures in the next book in S.M. Stirling’s Nantucket series: Against the Tide of Years. </span>
  <a data-text-id="3468705126847615250" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_426708975" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/426708975" />
    <a title="Richard" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1662632-richard"><img alt="Richard" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1540855273p2/1662632.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/426708975?book_show_action=true">Oct 02, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Richard" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Richard" href="/user/show/1662632-richard">Richard</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1662632-richard?shelf=fantasy-alt-history">fantasy-alt-history</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1662632-richard?shelf=series">series</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1662632-richard?shelf=scifi">scifi</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1662632-richard?shelf=scifi-time-travel">scifi-time-travel</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer426708975" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17384804326842399119">This is probably a pretty good book within the subgenre of time-travel/alternate-history, but that is damning with faint praise. There are so many pitfalls that have to be avoided that it usually isn't worth bothering to open the book.<br/><br/><i>(The only one I can recommend: <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/40293.Pastwatch_The_Redemption_of_Christopher_Columbus' title='Pastwatch The Redemption of Christopher Columbus by Orson Scott Card' rel='nofollow noopener'>Pastwatch: The Redemption of Christopher Columbus</a>. If you'll settle for just alternate-history, try the incredible <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/216363.The_Man_in_the_High_Castle' title='The Man in the High Castle by Philip K. Dick' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Man in the High Castle</a>, or for just time-travel, maybe the almost-incredible <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/24983.Doomsday_Book__Oxford_Time_Travel___1_' title='Doomsday Book (Oxford Time Travel, #1) by Connie Willis' rel='nofollow noopener'>Doomsday Book</a>.)</i><br/><br/>The biggest problem her</span>
  <span id="freeText17384804326842399119" style="display:none">This is probably a pretty good book within the subgenre of time-travel/alternate-history, but that is damning with faint praise. There are so many pitfalls that have to be avoided that it usually isn't worth bothering to open the book.<br /><br /><i>(The only one I can recommend: <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/40293.Pastwatch_The_Redemption_of_Christopher_Columbus" title="Pastwatch The Redemption of Christopher Columbus by Orson Scott Card" rel="nofollow noopener">Pastwatch: The Redemption of Christopher Columbus</a>. If you'll settle for just alternate-history, try the incredible <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/216363.The_Man_in_the_High_Castle" title="The Man in the High Castle by Philip K. Dick" rel="nofollow noopener">The Man in the High Castle</a>, or for just time-travel, maybe the almost-incredible <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/24983.Doomsday_Book__Oxford_Time_Travel___1_" title="Doomsday Book (Oxford Time Travel, #1) by Connie Willis" rel="nofollow noopener">Doomsday Book</a>.)</i><br /><br />The biggest problem here is that Stirling wanted the intrepid Nantucketeers to survive and thrive, and that is absurdly unlikely. Take an island of roughly 10,000 folks and toss them a few millennia back in time, and most will be dead within a year. If any descendants survive, they'll be indistinguishable from the natives of that era within two or maybe three generations.<br /><br />Why? Even if all of those 10,000 were highly intelligent and able-bodied adults, there are simply not enough to fill all the productive roles in any semblance of a modern economy.<br /><br />To even <i>begin</i> to reverse those odds, Stirling has to give his doughty islanders an astonishing array of expertise as well as some world-class machine tools. But the trump, of course, is that one of the two Coast Guard <i>sailing</i> ships just happens to be training in the neighborhood and comes with them, along with its crew and 150 cadets. Yes, that would be the real-world <a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/USCGC_Eagle_(WIX-327)" rel="nofollow noopener">USCGC Eagle</a>. Also impressive is the fact that not one, but two! officers on board are experts at sword fighting.<br /><br />Even with these advantages, their many bronze-age escapades are only possible with massive doses of luck and omissions of some hazards. Cross-cultural miscommunication turns out to be not a problem at all! Navigation to distant waters is a snap, even without GPS! One of the Coast Guard officers remembers — without notes! — everything necessary regarding how to design and build the kind of wooden sailing ship ideal for the situation. (Was it a carrack or a caravel? Can't remember).<br /><br />And that is, of course, the problem. The author has to give all the important characters too much skill (or too many skills) so they can deal with the vast variety of problems they'd face. A few disposable characters are tossed in to try to disguise this, but it isn't a problem that can really be hidden.<br /><br />On the other hand, the central character was a hoot. Hmmm, a black lesbian Coast Guard captain with advanced training with her beloved samurai sword? Honestly, take her out of this book and make her a movie action hero. Unfortunately, she was wasted here.<br /><br />The villain, sadly, isn't memorable at all. Wafer-thin character development, with nothing more to drive his nastiness than arrogance and glory-seeking. A little nuance might have helped — he could, instead, have wanted the islanders to conquer and rule the bronze age with benevolence and the hindsight of three millennia, putting him conflict with those wanting to lead by democratic example. No such luck. (Honestly, I would have bet against the democrat folks, since the underlying necessity of trusted institutions would have been absence, rendering "democracy" no more than a rubber-stamp for tyranny by a tribal majority, happy to be sanctified by elections while abusing their vile opponents. We see enough of that in the 21st century.)<br /><br />Oh, yeah: a number of other reviews here have lambasted this book for "deviant sexuality". I'm a San Franciscan, so I'm pretty hard to shock, but nothing here was <i>outré</i> enough to raise an eyebrow. One superfluous character goes in for extreme masochism amounting to torture, but the acts themselves are left to the imagination. That the author chose to add such an unlikely and grating aspect to the story was really no more than more evidence that the story just isn't very good.<br /><br />Not recommended. Unless you're really into this kinda stuff, which means you already are pretty tolerant of many of these kinds of problems.<br />­</span>
  <a data-text-id="17384804326842399119" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_215182039" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/215182039" />
    <a title="Kim" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4026072-kim"><img alt="Kim" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1458609397p2/4026072.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/215182039?book_show_action=true">Sep 25, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kim" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kim" href="/user/show/4026072-kim">Kim</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/8219648-island-in-the-sea-of-time">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4026072-kim?shelf=sci-fi">sci-fi</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4026072-kim?shelf=adventure">adventure</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4026072-kim?shelf=book-club-scifi-and-fantasy">book-club-scifi-and-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4026072-kim?shelf=action">action</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4026072-kim?shelf=book-club">book-club</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4026072-kim?shelf=time-travel">time-travel</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4026072-kim?shelf=male-author">male-author</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4026072-kim?shelf=historical">historical</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4026072-kim?shelf=alternate-history">alternate-history</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4026072-kim?shelf=1990s">1990s</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer215182039" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3232037713865817489">Wow. I had this book on my to-read shelf for some time as I'd heard it was a good alt history book but I never got around to reading it til one of my book clubs picked it as a series read. And I'm glad I finally read it.<br/><br/>A fascinating, thrilling story of an incident which send the island of Nantucket, MA, USA (plus a sailing vessel of the Coast Guard) back in time to around 1250 BC. The affected having to come to terms with the loss of everyone and everything they once knew and learn to live in t</span>
  <span id="freeText3232037713865817489" style="display:none">Wow. I had this book on my to-read shelf for some time as I'd heard it was a good alt history book but I never got around to reading it til one of my book clubs picked it as a series read. And I'm glad I finally read it.<br /><br />A fascinating, thrilling story of an incident which send the island of Nantucket, MA, USA (plus a sailing vessel of the Coast Guard) back in time to around 1250 BC. The affected having to come to terms with the loss of everyone and everything they once knew and learn to live in the Bronze Age.<br /><br />Now I will admit there is a lot of handwaving here. It seems to be amazing luck that they have fishermen, farmers, blacksmiths, historians, anthropologists, a vast array of people who know how to make or find everything required to get a society running at at least Industrial Revolution standards. But you know what? I didn't care. It meant the book kept moving and didn't end after two chapters with everyone dying. Which is what would happen if 9000 random people from my city were sent back to the past.<br /><br />I loved the little details of the civilisations of the time. I wanted to see more interactions and explorations but I believe that will occur in the rest of the series. This book really was about getting the Islanders to a stable point from which they could be self-sufficient plus the breakaway groups. <br /><br />There were times that I wish this book was written at a higher level though like <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/666256.Opening_Atlantis__Atlantis___1_" title="Opening Atlantis (Atlantis, #1) by Harry Turtledove" rel="nofollow noopener">Opening Atlantis</a> or <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/29579.Foundation__Foundation___1_" title="Foundation (Foundation, #1) by Isaac Asimov" rel="nofollow noopener">Foundation</a>, spanning generations to see what changes the Event caused. Especially, and this ties in with something that bugged me, when they were getting close to year 0. So here's something I really disliked. After everything else going ok, yeah sure existing tribes and civilisations would be completely changed but they had to survive somehow, they decide to unleash Christianity on the locals. A religion based on someone who wouldn't even be "born" for over 1000 years. I guess they at least might get a coming of Jesus. But I wouldn't have thought the scientists who were helping oversee would have just allowed that through without some challenge. <br /><br />Though they were all thrown thousands of years into the past by an unknown force. Maybe that's a good time to start praying to someone.<br /><br />One of the other points I really loved was the questions and implications raised by such an event. Should they have tried to live a completely isolationist existence? They had to resort to whaling for oil and food and other by-products, but was that a bad thing in a time when whale populations would be immense and sustainable hunting could be enacted from day 1? <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[I understand needing to help the local British inhabitants protect themselves from a force lead by an American but was the wholesale slaughter and hatred of the Olmecs necessary? The way they talked about eradicating them was akin to genocide. Plus destroying the Olmec culture would lead to their being no Aztecs or Mayans or any other Central/South American civilisations. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />This was a great book. History was always my favourite subject and I would love the chance to live it for myself. Though could I really give up all the modern luxuries? Who knows. I can't wait to read the next book.</span>
  <a data-text-id="3232037713865817489" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2151543948" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2151543948?book_show_action=true">Oct 21, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="YouKneeK" class="user" itemprop="url" name="YouKneeK" href="/user/show/25923230-youkneek">YouKneeK</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/8219648-island-in-the-sea-of-time">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/25923230-youkneek?shelf=completed-series">completed-series</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/25923230-youkneek?shelf=alternate-history">alternate-history</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2151543948" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10914951069382598691">This is an alternate history in which the island of Nantucket is unexpectedly and inexplicably thrown back in time from 1998 to 1250 B.C. Nantucket is a real island, part of Massachusetts in the U.S. The story focuses on how they survive, considering Nantucket had relied mostly on outside food sources. They also needed raw materials that were limited in supply in order to make various goods, tools, and weapons, and politics are involved as they decide how to rule their island and how to handle t</span>
  <span id="freeText10914951069382598691" style="display:none">This is an alternate history in which the island of Nantucket is unexpectedly and inexplicably thrown back in time from 1998 to 1250 B.C. Nantucket is a real island, part of Massachusetts in the U.S. The story focuses on how they survive, considering Nantucket had relied mostly on outside food sources. They also needed raw materials that were limited in supply in order to make various goods, tools, and weapons, and politics are involved as they decide how to rule their island and how to handle the distribution of labor and supplies. A Coast Guard ship was conveniently near the island at the time of the event, so it was caught in the past too, providing a valuable resource for seeking trade among the natives of both North America and England. <br /><br />Most of the story held my interest. I liked the political parts, and seeing what they had to do to survive, and I loved the parts where they met native cultures for the first time and learned about each other. There were times, though, when I started to lose interest and got bogged down in details that didn’t interest me as much. The event that caused them to be thrown back in time is never explained. There’s some speculation in the beginning, but nothing remotely close to a real answer. I don’t know if it will be addressed later in the trilogy, but my impression so far is that it was just the vehicle for the story the author wanted to tell and probably not something that will ever be dealt with in detail.<br /><br />As a side note, the Kindle edition I have has erratic section breaks. Sometimes there were section breaks in the form of a little extra line spacing, and sometimes there weren’t any breaks at all and it wasn’t always immediately clear that the setting had changed.<br /><br />I’m giving this 3.5 stars on sites where I can give half stars, and rounding up to 4 on Goodreads. I enjoyed it well enough to try the second book in the series.</span>
  <a data-text-id="10914951069382598691" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText17792597115847831880" style="display:none">In a word, terrible.<br /><br />In several words, racist, sexist, and just problematic in more ways than one. <br /><br />The ones concerned about having supremely negative effects on the current civilizations are the ones that are delusional, incompetent, and lead to failure.<br /><br />The sole mentioned Asian-American character is a woman who gets her rocks off by torturing people. <br /><br />The black woman who is in charge of the coast guard people stranded with the island and is part of the closest thing they have to a military is a lesbian.<br /><br />One of the other few black people with the Nantucketers is so, so terribly obsessed with Black Egyptians and Black African Supremacy. <br /><br />The two Jewish people are paired up with each other.<br /><br />All of the unmarried and childless women are quickly paired off with someone for purposes of procreation. <br /><br />There's also the fetish for martial arts and Japanese swords and armor that practically all of the characters, regardless of their background, possess. <br /><br />I was hoping for something along the same lines as 1632, but instead I found an awful book filled with terrible fetishes, awful stereotypes, and characters that can do no wrong if they're the protagonists. </span>

<div id="review_377057715" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/377057715" />
    <a title="Sara" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4275212-sara"><img alt="Sara" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1418613089p2/4275212.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/377057715?book_show_action=true">Jul 25, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sara" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sara" href="/user/show/4275212-sara">Sara</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4275212-sara?shelf=fish-in-the-sea">fish-in-the-sea</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer377057715" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10280286101029448889">I give credit to Stirling for making such an accurate time travel story and for clearly doing his research, making it as realistic as possible. However, that's one of the only satisfactions I received. Eventually said research became overbearing, and instead of letting his readers learn and come to understand the world through the lives of their characters he resorted to info-dumping in excruciating detail, and often in the most annoying places. There would be numerous times in the middle of cha</span>
  <span id="freeText10280286101029448889" style="display:none">I give credit to Stirling for making such an accurate time travel story and for clearly doing his research, making it as realistic as possible. However, that's one of the only satisfactions I received. Eventually said research became overbearing, and instead of letting his readers learn and come to understand the world through the lives of their characters he resorted to info-dumping in excruciating detail, and often in the most annoying places. There would be numerous times in the middle of character interaction he would pause and proceed to explain in one to three long paragraphs things happening that were of no real interest (how a machine works, how a ship is built, what's needed to feed a couple thousand people, etc.), taking you briefly out of the story. There were also times where he would dedicate an entire scene to characters talking about how such-and-such works. No relevance to the story whatsoever.<br /><br />You don't get a whole lot of feel for the characters either. They're all pretty much shadowed by this drivel. Except, perhaps, Marian Alston, which I found to be a likeable character. The rest of them were boring with no inner dilemma to make them seem more real and even less outer drama with each other. Unless, of course, you were a "bad person". The "bad people" were basically anyone who disagreed with the main characters, whether it was to an extreme and they wished for physical harm, or if they just had different beliefs. Please. I only buy into the black and white characterization with children's book because it's something children can understand. I let that pass. By the time you're writing adult fiction, however, I think you should have enough experience in life to be able to write characters who are not all good or all bad. People have faults and make mistakes, even if they do good things. And guess what, not all people who oppose them are evil.<br /><br />It's sad because I think he could have done a lot with the story itself and the characters had it not been something of a "circle of friends" with a lot of unnecessary information crammed in.</span>
  <a data-text-id="10280286101029448889" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer1670431121228018609">I loved this book, and the two that followed in the trilogy. <br/><br/>Quick synopsis - the island of Nantucket (and a wooden Coast Guard ship) are mysteriously whisked back in time several thousand years. <br/><br/>The only reason I didn't give this one five stars is that Stirling gets a bit carried away with some of the more ... unsavory sexual behavior of some of his characters. This seems to be a consistent trend of his in most of his books. He can't seem to write plain old vanilla sex - his sex scenes are eith</span>
  <span id="freeText1670431121228018609" style="display:none">I loved this book, and the two that followed in the trilogy. <br /><br />Quick synopsis - the island of Nantucket (and a wooden Coast Guard ship) are mysteriously whisked back in time several thousand years. <br /><br />The only reason I didn't give this one five stars is that Stirling gets a bit carried away with some of the more ... unsavory sexual behavior of some of his characters. This seems to be a consistent trend of his in most of his books. He can't seem to write plain old vanilla sex - his sex scenes are either of lesbian and/or EXTREMELY brutal acts of sadism. </span>
  <a data-text-id="1670431121228018609" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1285194535" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4531474926742294602">For a guy who makes such a point of writing characters against stereotypes, S.M. Stirling sure writes a lot ethnic stereotypes. Seriously, this thing reads like a collaboration between Andrea Dworkin and Sax Rohmer.<br/><br/>I have a lot to say about the plot, but honestly that would apply to the genre as a whole. If you think a bunch of modern first worlders with a representative (and extremely unlikely) cross-section of skills and understanding of modern technology inexplicably go back in time to impose</span>
  <span id="freeText4531474926742294602" style="display:none">For a guy who makes such a point of writing characters against stereotypes, S.M. Stirling sure writes a lot ethnic stereotypes. Seriously, this thing reads like a collaboration between Andrea Dworkin and Sax Rohmer.<br /><br />I have a lot to say about the plot, but honestly that would apply to the genre as a whole. If you think a bunch of modern first worlders with a representative (and extremely unlikely) cross-section of skills and understanding of modern technology inexplicably go back in time to impose middle of the road American values on those barbarians in the past is a super cool idea you might not hate this as much as I did.</span>

<div id="review_2087015456" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2087015456" />
    <a title="Carolyn F." class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2624012-carolyn-f"><img alt="Carolyn F." src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1521926478p2/2624012.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2087015456?book_show_action=true">Sep 18, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Carolyn F." class="user" itemprop="url" name="Carolyn F." href="/user/show/2624012-carolyn-f">Carolyn F.</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="MP3 Book 9781400176793" href="/book/show/11035384-island-in-the-sea-of-time">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2624012-carolyn-f?shelf=audiobook">audiobook</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2624012-carolyn-f?shelf=sci-fi">sci-fi</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2624012-carolyn-f?shelf=historical">historical</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2624012-carolyn-f?shelf=library-book-club">library-book-club</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2087015456" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1336583448857525593"><b>Audiobook</b><br/><br/>Can a book about a modern day island on the American east coast (Nantucket) going back in time be boring? Yes. And for an isolated island with minimal supplies there is a lot of traveling going on - to Europe, to the Caribbean, South America. I know the author didn't want to bog down the book with descriptions of days and days of travel, but sometimes it seemed they were one day in Nantucket and then after waiting a week (no real sense of urgency - just we're going as fast as we can?!),</span>
  <span id="freeText1336583448857525593" style="display:none"><b>Audiobook</b><br /><br />Can a book about a modern day island on the American east coast (Nantucket) going back in time be boring? Yes. And for an isolated island with minimal supplies there is a lot of traveling going on - to Europe, to the Caribbean, South America. I know the author didn't want to bog down the book with descriptions of days and days of travel, but sometimes it seemed they were one day in Nantucket and then after waiting a week (no real sense of urgency - just we're going as fast as we can?!), it would take them about a day or so to get to the baddies. <br /><br />And I'm sick of reading that every battle between native and more civilized forces being compared to the Anglo-Zulu War. Catherine Asaro did a much better job with a comparison of this conflict. The "final" battle was confusing because I kept thinking, "Are they with the Eagle people or the Wolf people?" <br /><br />Anyway, I didn't enjoy this book much at all.</span>
  <a data-text-id="1336583448857525593" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_138110745" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/138110745" />
    <a title="Chak" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/962423-chak"><img alt="Chak" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1204567065p2/962423.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/138110745?book_show_action=true">Jan 03, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Chak" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Chak" href="/user/show/962423-chak">Chak</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Chak by: </span>
      Claire
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/962423-chak?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/962423-chak?shelf=sci-fi-and-fantasy">sci-fi-and-fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer138110745" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3566517590613331552">I was completely hooked by the plot, but the writing and character development brought the rating down a few points. The Island of Nantucket (with all of the people, buildings, ships and technology within a certain radius) was mysteriously sent back in time to the year 1200 B.C. The most interesting parts of the book for me were the efforts to form a government and society and provide continued sustenance and safety of the people. Stirling reasoned through all of this very well, and when he stuc</span>
  <span id="freeText3566517590613331552" style="display:none">I was completely hooked by the plot, but the writing and character development brought the rating down a few points. The Island of Nantucket (with all of the people, buildings, ships and technology within a certain radius) was mysteriously sent back in time to the year 1200 B.C. The most interesting parts of the book for me were the efforts to form a government and society and provide continued sustenance and safety of the people. Stirling reasoned through all of this very well, and when he stuck to logistics, he was brilliant. Also, I loved the character of Marion Alston, a formidable woman who goes from being a stoic, modern leader to a righteous and nearly invulnerable warrior. As a protagonist, she's easy to root for and clearly likable, though her stoic nature keeps her from dwelling on too much of her inner conflict, which is a bit regrettable since she could have been even more complex. The antagonist William Walker is one-dimensional and falls flat even next to the subdued dimensionality of Alston. Compare the simplicity of Walker to an almost perfectly complex villain such as (the reimagined) Battlestar Galactica's Gaius Baltar and the difference is clear. Waging war on a relatively effective (plot-wise) but otherwise shallow villain (and his ridiculously cliche sidekick Alice Hong) actually degrades the protagonist and she deserved a better literary experience.<br /><br />Also, the characters and plot are subordinate to writer's conceit in that over-exposition and frivolous outpouring of unnecessary details are used in place of development (see ship-rigging, metal working, how much a human "voids" when he/she dies, etc.). Don't get me wrong, the details would have been fine if they were used in addition to development, instead of in place of it. Along those same lines, the sexual violence is a simple shortcut to outrage and procuring emotional investment instead of courting it with depth of character and good writing. <br /><br />The "event" of going back in time is never explained or even really considered much by the characters in the book, which was odd, to say the least. This book is the first in a three-book series that follows the exploits of these characters and is loosely tied to a much larger series by the same author that starts with "Dies the Fire" and basically tells the story of the people who were not on the Island of Nantucket and who therefore did not go back in time. I believe it's in the sixth book in that series that the reader finds out what caused the "event." I read a spoiler and thought the explanation was a cop-out, so I decided to cut my losses here and not read further, as the explanation of the "event" was the only thing I was really curious about after being so disappointed by other facets of the story. </span>
  <a data-text-id="3566517590613331552" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/17766893-matty-swytla?shelf=chunkster-challenge">chunkster-challenge</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/17766893-matty-swytla?shelf=time-travel">time-travel</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/17766893-matty-swytla?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/17766893-matty-swytla?shelf=bralnica-2018">bralnica-2018</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/17766893-matty-swytla?shelf=series">series</a>,

          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2445081486" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1769891158205354284">Now this book was just right for my reading taste - time travel, competent people pulling through, enough history to enjoy the differences, and some action. Not everything is smooth sailing, and some characters need more work to be completely fleshed out, but it's a solid 4 stars. Of course there some serious gore and over-all shitty handling of women in the hands of past men, but there's enough of positive energy that things are going to change to be eager to read more.<br/><br/>Reading some of the more </span>
  <span id="freeText1769891158205354284" style="display:none">Now this book was just right for my reading taste - time travel, competent people pulling through, enough history to enjoy the differences, and some action. Not everything is smooth sailing, and some characters need more work to be completely fleshed out, but it's a solid 4 stars. Of course there some serious gore and over-all shitty handling of women in the hands of past men, but there's enough of positive energy that things are going to change to be eager to read more.<br /><br />Reading some of the more popular (negative) reviews, I'm slightly puzzled by all the contemporary feminism and social justice people nag about. Am I missing something? There's enough competent women and people of colour in this book to satisfy this demanding bunch. As to reasons why you don't want to sail to Africa right away - erm, ever heard of the nice tropical diseases over there? Maybe some issues with water and wind currents? But also - fresh water and food are a problem too, not to mention natural harbors in case of really bad weather. Why do you think even behemoth tankers go down these days?<br /><br />So, I think the author did a splendid job for the first book in this series, and set up a fantastic basis for next adventures and culture clash. I do hope some bad characters meet their deserved end sometime soon, though. Really, Walker and Hong? World domination and torture? Go get them Alston.</span>
  <a data-text-id="1769891158205354284" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

  <span id="freeText14690703027408191908" style="display:none">I picked this up as an audio book, a set of 21 CDs, at a book sale some time ago. I listened to the first 9 CDs mostly on a bit of a road trip, but when I got home my fragmented 10-20 minute drives just weren't as conducive to audiobook listening. At that point in the story, I was only halfway engaged. I wanted to know how it ended, but not badly enough to listen through another 12 hours over the course of many weeks. So I skipped to the last CD, and I'm sure I missed some cool stuff, but I feel like I got the gist of it well enough.<br /><br />I loved the way this book captured so many island character types. I don't live on Nantucket, but I do live on the island next door, and they felt pretty true to life. The martial arts bits that came in were also pretty good. I liked a lot of the characters. It was a good story, but I guess I'm just not in the mood for really long books right now. </span>

<div id="review_195221240" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/195221240" />
    <a title="Hikachi" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5314285-hikachi"><img alt="Hikachi" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1303701244p2/5314285.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/195221240?book_show_action=true">Aug 06, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Hikachi" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Hikachi" href="/user/show/5314285-hikachi">Hikachi</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5314285-hikachi?shelf=adventure">adventure</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer195221240&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer195221240" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2204096735384417241">When a friend suggested this book to me, I have to admit that I sort of attracted by the idea. Yes, I haven't read much stories about time travel. Stranded, maybe, but time travel and stranded. This was my first time.<br/><br/>The first few chapters were engaging, for me. The plot was built in a superbly easy to understand way. A whole Nantucket Island was transported to the 1200 BC. Along with a ship and her crew that was (unfortunately) around the same area.<br/><br/>So they had to survive, okay, and also work on</span>
  <span id="freeText2204096735384417241" style="display:none">When a friend suggested this book to me, I have to admit that I sort of attracted by the idea. Yes, I haven't read much stories about time travel. Stranded, maybe, but time travel and stranded. This was my first time.<br /><br />The first few chapters were engaging, for me. The plot was built in a superbly easy to understand way. A whole Nantucket Island was transported to the 1200 BC. Along with a ship and her crew that was (unfortunately) around the same area.<br /><br />So they had to survive, okay, and also work on their knowledge about the era, understandable, do adapt, well yeah... Occasional sex out of convenience... Huh what? At first, the sex scene was already made me twitch with uncertainty if I should continue read this book or put it in my half-read list with no definite date when I'll continue it. Anyhow, the first sex scene I encountered was kind of okay, it wasn't explicit or took a whole chapter describing the whole action. But after a few pages, there's another sex scene. And another one, and another one, and another one. Those weren't explicit, yes, but they're really annoying cause it happened without any significant meaning for the story.<br /><br />Another thing that irked me was the characterization. Bland, black and white much, cardboard-like. The characters were as bad as those written/created by Stephenie Meyer and Cassandra Clare. There's no inner conflict, and the external conflict was kept to minimum. I guess it's because the idea of "how to survive" could be pretty overwhelming for one, and too good to be the main conflict.<br />The villain was simply pure evil who boasted his evilness, while the good guys are goody two shoes much. Hello?! True to the word "fiction", I believe. <br /><br />I gave this book 1.7 actually, but since goodreads has no decimals, I had to give it two stars. The only good thing is the idea of time travel and some history research. And also how the author seemed to have done a profound research about bronze age. Otherwise, I don't really recommend it.</span>
  <a data-text-id="2204096735384417241" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_601955930" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/601955930" />
    <a title="David" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/155663-david"><img alt="David" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1581956036p2/155663.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/601955930?book_show_action=true">Apr 28, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="David" class="user" itemprop="url" name="David" href="/user/show/155663-david">David</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/155663-david?shelf=audiobook">audiobook</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/155663-david?shelf=speculative-fiction">speculative-fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer601955930" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17867682886620646429">This is a good swash-buckling adventure story. The island of Nantucket is suddenly swept into the year 1250 BCE, along with the Coast Guard vessel "Eagle" which happens to be sailing nearby. While the storyline is good, it is too predictable. Soon after each main character is introduced, it is all too obvious how that character would be faring in the story.<br/><br/>Apart from the small reserves held on Nantucket from before the time switch, petro-chemicals are not available. Therefore, electricity and mo</span>
  <span id="freeText17867682886620646429" style="display:none">This is a good swash-buckling adventure story. The island of Nantucket is suddenly swept into the year 1250 BCE, along with the Coast Guard vessel "Eagle" which happens to be sailing nearby. While the storyline is good, it is too predictable. Soon after each main character is introduced, it is all too obvious how that character would be faring in the story.<br /><br />Apart from the small reserves held on Nantucket from before the time switch, petro-chemicals are not available. Therefore, electricity and most modes of transport are very limited. It is interesting to see how modern people cope with these limitations to develop--or re-invent--old methods for increasing productivity. They manage to re-invent a modern civilization, subject to the constraints of the bronze age. <br /><br />Interestingly, the main character is a lesbian Afro-American woman, who is the highly-skilled captain of the Eagle. Her knowledge of nautical affairs, human psychology, martial arts and tactical warfare are crucial to the well-being of the Nantucket colony. If anything, she seems to be too capable to be realistic--but realism is not the point of this book! It is also very interesting how a few characters with modern politically-correct leanings, point themselves toward destruction, as they are oblivious to the vastly different viewpoints of people who grow up in the bronze age.</span>
  <a data-text-id="17867682886620646429" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3222446-libby?shelf=unforgettable">unforgettable</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3222446-libby?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer87399519" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13418356292579830570">I have been rereading old favorites this summer, and I am happy to say that most of them are as enjoyable as I remembered. This one was filed in my mind as a swashbuckling adventure in time travel. I recalled it as being super engaging, keeping my nose firmly in the book through a long and eventful weekend of travel. Well, my memories were accurate and I can still say that nobody does it better than S.M. Stirling. In this one, he moves the island of Nantucket from now into the Bronze Age. The in</span>
  <span id="freeText13418356292579830570" style="display:none">I have been rereading old favorites this summer, and I am happy to say that most of them are as enjoyable as I remembered. This one was filed in my mind as a swashbuckling adventure in time travel. I recalled it as being super engaging, keeping my nose firmly in the book through a long and eventful weekend of travel. Well, my memories were accurate and I can still say that nobody does it better than S.M. Stirling. In this one, he moves the island of Nantucket from now into the Bronze Age. The inhabitants are cut off from power, thrown onto their own resources, forced to adjust, be flexible, adapt and figure out how to feed themselves in a world they don't know and don't control. It is fast paced and full of action. The characters are fully realized, believable folks with talents and flaws. Stirling has the knack of sliding his readers into his story and riveting their attention to the action. He writes with wit and empathy, causing us to feel that we are right there with the characters. I loved this story back when, and I love it still. I think you will love it as well.</span>
  <a data-text-id="13418356292579830570" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">

        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/72922814?book_show_action=true">Sep 29, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer72922814" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12247330871287702659">Disappointing. I loved the premise of this book (modern Americans sent back in time, need to cope and rebuild society) but the sex and race stuff was just ick, and the violence was unappealing. I found the rape scenes really disturbing and wish they had not been included. While Stirling is great at thinking through the hows of this situation, some of his characters and scenes are so hard to take that I ended up skimming whole sections. I appreciate that the leads were not all straight white men,</span>
  <span id="freeText12247330871287702659" style="display:none">Disappointing. I loved the premise of this book (modern Americans sent back in time, need to cope and rebuild society) but the sex and race stuff was just ick, and the violence was unappealing. I found the rape scenes really disturbing and wish they had not been included. While Stirling is great at thinking through the hows of this situation, some of his characters and scenes are so hard to take that I ended up skimming whole sections. I appreciate that the leads were not all straight white men, but I wish that the lesbian couple was not treated so voyeristically, especially when compared to the white heterosexual couples. <br /><br />Bad sign: I actually put the book down in the middle of a climactic scene, and didn't pick it up again for a week.<br />Good sign: I will probably pick the next two books up at the library next time I notice them on the shelf, because I'm sort of curious about how the cross cultural interactions continue.</span>
  <a data-text-id="12247330871287702659" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

  <span id="freeText9529046559851310427" style="display:none">3.5 stars. Excellent, if you like Swiss Family Robinson and Connecticut Yankee in King Arthur's Court-type stories. Well-researched and told.<br /><br />But it was all too quick and too easy. Yeah, there was a big conflict of sorts, but everything worked too well for even the renegade "Islanders." But isn't that the style of these back-to-the-past stories?<br /><br />Fun read. Not great literature. Hardly even credible, despite all the research Stirling apparently did. <br /><br />Heavy-handed negative stereotypes among secondary characters, assumedly to define (and enhance) the main characters.<br /><br />Ended without closure on many major issues. That's why it got such a low rating.<br /><br />If I'd known it was, despite being 608 pages long, just "volume one" of a series, I might not have bought it.)</span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer992028784" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17803031855359724655"> This book had/has the potential to get bogged down in the details. Part of the whole alternate history/time travel allure is everything we take for granted in the modern world that doesn't exist in this setting. The down side is that you can get lost in describing all the re-invention you have to do to the detriment of the story. Stirling rides a pretty good line creating a story with drama that you want to keep reading and having the speculative details add to the story.<br/><br/> One of the main charac</span>
  <span id="freeText17803031855359724655" style="display:none"> This book had/has the potential to get bogged down in the details. Part of the whole alternate history/time travel allure is everything we take for granted in the modern world that doesn't exist in this setting. The down side is that you can get lost in describing all the re-invention you have to do to the detriment of the story. Stirling rides a pretty good line creating a story with drama that you want to keep reading and having the speculative details add to the story.<br /><br /> One of the main characters was a bit overdone, one too many outsider aspects to her characterization to really be believable but it wasn't so bad it affected me much. The book was good enough that I want to read the sequals but not so good I am running out and getting others to read it.<br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="17803031855359724655" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('SDsAKoiEGis1Us6vgzR1SlPhz0LHkcE9tjeXrywpUUri3k2ufqn5Bm8F8x2I/xX0D2h1ycLTJGBh+xwWYyZ8sw==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('jmaydNLC1tj+Smp6DZU73VZLbBnpebR1hTxGzkLZDtMkg//wJO819aQdV8gGXltjCsLWkuw7UShS8M13DdYjKg==')})
  }

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer8534051185278665356">Stephen Michael Stirling is a French-born Canadian-American science fiction and fantasy author. Stirling is probably best known for his <i>Draka</i> series of alternate history novels and the more recent time travel/alternate history <i>Nantucket</i> series and <i>Emberverse</i> series.<br/><br/>MINI AUTO-BIOGRAPHY:<br/>(personal website: source)<br/><br/>I’m a writer by trade, born in France but Canadian by origin and American by naturalizat</span>
  <span id="freeText8534051185278665356" style="display:none">Stephen Michael Stirling is a French-born Canadian-American science fiction and fantasy author. Stirling is probably best known for his <i>Draka</i> series of alternate history novels and the more recent time travel/alternate history <i>Nantucket</i> series and <i>Emberverse</i> series.<br /><br />MINI AUTO-BIOGRAPHY:<br />(personal website: source)<br /><br />I’m a writer by trade, born in France but Canadian by origin and American by naturalization, living in New Mexico at present. My hobbies are mostly related to the craft? I love history, anthropology and archaeology, and am interested in the sciences. The martial arts are my main physical hobby.<br /><br /></span>
